<div id="review_1219004305" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1219004305" />
    <a title="Hana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10571559-hana"><img alt="Hana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1458172215p2/10571559.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1219004305?book_show_action=true">Mar 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hana" href="/user/show/10571559-hana">Hana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10571559-hana?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10571559-hana?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10571559-hana?shelf=18th-19th-century">18th-19th-century</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10571559-hana?shelf=2015-reads">2015-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1219004305" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3658878540679006909">The literary equivalent of those marvelous British period dramas with utterly glorious settings and luscious costumes.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426258984i/13993974._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I can never resist this sort thing. Pages of details of soft white brocades, ruffle upon ruffle, falling over great hoops, auburn hair piled in elaborate curls, pearls against soft pale skin, and perfect accessories like...chicken-skin fans. <br/><br/>And since this is 18th century France before the Revolution, the men are just as gorgeous and even more colorful....<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426258984i/13993975._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>When we first meet the h</span>
  <span id="freeText3658878540679006909" style="display:none">The literary equivalent of those marvelous British period dramas with utterly glorious settings and luscious costumes.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426258984i/13993974._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I can never resist this sort thing. Pages of details of soft white brocades, ruffle upon ruffle, falling over great hoops, auburn hair piled in elaborate curls, pearls against soft pale skin, and perfect accessories like...chicken-skin fans. <br><br>And since this is 18th century France before the Revolution, the men are just as gorgeous and even more colorful....<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426258984i/13993975._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>When we first meet the hero, the Duke of Avon, he is arrayed "in a full-skirted coat of purple satin, heavily laced with gold," his wig immaculately powdered, carrying a beribboned cane, and mincing along in high heels. The Duke is returning to his palatial Paris hôtel from a night of gaming or perhaps other amusements when an urchin stumbles across his path and begs for help: "Great violet-blue eyes gazed wildly up at him, terror in their depths." <br><br>This is a Georgette Heyer romance so we all know where this is going, but getting there is splendid fun. The plot is a lively but improbable mix of The Count of Monte Cristo and My Fair Lady yet it's all so glittering that I hardly noticed the plot holes as I gawked at ballroom scenes at Versailles and yearned to own one marvelous gown after another. <br><br>The descriptions are splendid, the dialog witty, and the protagonists are likable, particularly the little urchin who is transformed into....well that <i>would</i> be telling! <br><br>Along the way, we get to meet luminaries at the court of Louis V, including the famed courtesan, Madam Pompadour....<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426261143i/13994292._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>splendidly dressed, of course! <br><br>I've read most of Georgette Heyer's Regency romances, but I'm new to those set in 18th century France and England. You can be sure I'll be back for more! Read with fellow <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/2234572-these-old-shades-march-2015-chapters-1-18" rel="nofollow noopener">Georgette Heyer Fans</a> who added so much to the pleasure--thank you all! </span>
  <a data-text-id="3658878540679006909" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2117941089?book_show_action=true">Oct 30, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vivian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vivian" href="/user/show/3947172-vivian">Vivian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3947172-vivian?shelf=2017-odyssey">2017-odyssey</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3947172-vivian?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3947172-vivian?shelf=romance-hist">romance-hist</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2117941089" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14837621259146957439">GAH! I adore Georgian period romances. The ridiculous extravagance and theatricality of action and costume are simply divine. <br/><br/><b>
  <blockquote>"I thought you disliked melodrama, my friend?"<br/>"I do; but I have a veritable passion for--justice."<br/>"You've nourished thoughts of vengeance--for twenty years?"</blockquote>
</b><br/><br/>Other pluses which definitely made this a win: Heroine disguised as a boy, swordplay as well as hoydenish behaviors overlaid with a sweet naïveté; and an older sworn bachelor and renown rake charmed back into life</span>
  <span id="freeText14837621259146957439" style="display:none">GAH! I adore Georgian period romances. The ridiculous extravagance and theatricality of action and costume are simply divine. <br /><br /><b>
  <blockquote>"I thought you disliked melodrama, my friend?"<br />"I do; but I have a veritable passion for--justice."<br />"You've nourished thoughts of vengeance--for twenty years?"</blockquote>
</b><br /><br />Other pluses which definitely made this a win: Heroine disguised as a boy, swordplay as well as hoydenish behaviors overlaid with a sweet naïveté; and an older sworn bachelor and renown rake charmed back into life's pleasure from the malaise of ennui. It's Pygmalion with far more entertaining circumstances.<br /><br /><b>
  <blockquote>The button of her foil came to rest below his left shoulder. <br />"Touche," said Avon. "That was rather better, infant."<br />Leonie danced in her excitement.<br />"Monseigneur, I have killed you! You are dead! You are dead!"<br />"You display an unseemly joy," he remarked. "I had no notion you were so bloodthirsty."</blockquote>
</b> <br /><br />If you like historical romances, brats, and an age difference then you really can't go wrong, here. I feel rather silly that the title was so off-putting to me that I failed to read it earlier. And yes, I comprehended the ancient Greek concept of shade, but dismissed the opportunity. Rather stupid of me, to be honest. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14837621259146957439" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1910356" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1910356" />

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1910356?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trin" href="/user/show/113980-trin">Trin</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/113980-trin?shelf=historicalfiction">historicalfiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/113980-trin?shelf=english-lit">english-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/113980-trin?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/113980-trin?shelf=genderfuck">genderfuck</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1910356" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer39428412648155371">Most fandom people I've talked to either love or at least rather like this book, but it seems it's my turn to feel all "bwah?" and left out, as Punk does with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/452940.The_Dreyfus_Affair_A_Love_Story' title='The Dreyfus Affair A Love Story by Peter Lefcourt' rel='nofollow noopener'> The Dreyfus Affair</a> and Siria does with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/68485.Swordspoint__Riverside___1_' title='Swordspoint (Riverside, #1) by Ellen Kushner' rel='nofollow noopener'> Swordspoint</a>. I hated it. I despised pretty much all the characters, other than Hugh and Rupert—Leonie was irritating, and Avon was just creepy. I know he was supposed to be "Satanas"—the devil of a man who isn't really that bad, but I found him neither enjoyably naughty nor charming; he was just kin</span>
  <span id="freeText39428412648155371" style="display:none">Most fandom people I've talked to either love or at least rather like this book, but it seems it's my turn to feel all "bwah?" and left out, as Punk does with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/452940.The_Dreyfus_Affair_A_Love_Story" title="The Dreyfus Affair A Love Story by Peter Lefcourt" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Dreyfus Affair</a> and Siria does with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/68485.Swordspoint__Riverside___1_" title="Swordspoint (Riverside, #1) by Ellen Kushner" rel="nofollow noopener"> Swordspoint</a>. I hated it. I despised pretty much all the characters, other than Hugh and Rupert—Leonie was irritating, and Avon was just creepy. I know he was supposed to be "Satanas"—the devil of a man who isn't really that bad, but I found him neither enjoyably naughty nor charming; he was just kind of slimy. The idea of him and Leonie being together really skeeved me out, not because of the age difference—I actually <i>like</i> an age difference, when it's done well—but because of the power dynamic, I guess. All the power was Avon's, both practically and emotionally, and throughout the whole book Leonie was worshipful of him and he condescending towards her. Ew. I also didn't see the slash at all; Hugh was one of the few nice characters, as I said, so I guess it could be construed that he put up with Avon because he was in love with him, but Avon didn't seem particularly gay to me—he was just an 18th Century dude who lived in France and was a bit of a vain ass. The overall package was not appealing, and neither was this book, which is too bad, because I really enjoyed the only other Heyer I've read, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32109.The_Masqueraders" title="The Masqueraders by Georgette Heyer" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Masqueraders</a>.<br /><br />Before I read <i>These Old Shades</i>, I was planning to read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/261689.The_Grand_Sophy" title="The Grand Sophy by Georgette Heyer" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Grand Sophy</a> soon, but now I'm not so sure; <i>Shades</i> turned me off, and I also heard that <i>Sophy</i> has a really ugly Jewish stereotype in it. Those of you who've read it: what do you think?</span>
  <a data-text-id="39428412648155371" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1786454479" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1786454479" />
    <a title="Naksed" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29458352-naksed"><img alt="Naksed" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417804998p2/29458352.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1786454479?book_show_action=true">Oct 24, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Naksed" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Naksed" href="/user/show/29458352-naksed">Naksed</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29458352-naksed?shelf=may-december-romance">may-december-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29458352-naksed?shelf=18th-century">18th-century</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29458352-naksed?shelf=guardian-and-ward">guardian-and-ward</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29458352-naksed?shelf=manwhore-gets-the-virgin">manwhore-gets-the-virgin</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29458352-naksed?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29458352-naksed?shelf=implausible">implausible</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1786454479" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13115014323537088102">A guardian-ward romance set in the reign of Louis XV, with a dash of Pygmalion, and a revenge dish served very, very cold, Georgette Heyer's <i>These Old Shades</i> was quite delicious, once I was able to ignore and set aside the hopelessly out of touch and destructive hypothesis that is at the core of the novel. That is, nature will always win out over nurture. So if an aristocratic, well-bred, pure-blood being is unwittingly ripped from its natural surroundings and thrust upon a dung heap, it will st</span>
  <span id="freeText13115014323537088102" style="display:none">A guardian-ward romance set in the reign of Louis XV, with a dash of Pygmalion, and a revenge dish served very, very cold, Georgette Heyer's <i>These Old Shades</i> was quite delicious, once I was able to ignore and set aside the hopelessly out of touch and destructive hypothesis that is at the core of the novel. That is, nature will always win out over nurture. So if an aristocratic, well-bred, pure-blood being is unwittingly ripped from its natural surroundings and thrust upon a dung heap, it will still manage to bloom as a most radiant flower. And vice-versa, you can put lipstick on a pig and he always will reek. <br /><br />The dialogue and characterizations in this story were superb, particularly the male protagonist, a fortyish, dandified, rakehell of the Georgian era. The denouement of his meticulously planned revenge was so perfect that it made the comeuppance of the evil shrew of <i>Les Liasons Dangereuses</i> seem like child's play.<br /><br />I have to admit though that the cast of secondary characters, a madcap assortment of aristos with always a bon mot, a box of snuff, and an invitation to a ball up their sleeves, and the infantile, annoying heroine, who I am sure delighted the original readership of this book, kind of grated on me. <br /><br />Still, overall, an entertaining little book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13115014323537088102" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_410010594" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/410010594" />
    <a title="G." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5487874-g"><img alt="G." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1456934593p2/5487874.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/410010594?book_show_action=true">Sep 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="G." class="user" itemprop="url" name="G." href="/user/show/5487874-g">G.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer410010594" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12618332039828728138">I'm a fan of romance novels, especially historical, so I tend to read quite a bit of them. I know that Georgette Heyer is sort of a legend in this subgenre, but I have never read any of her books before now. I chose to read <i>These Old Shades</i> because it's part of a trilogy. I thought, hey, I'll read the three books and then decide what I think of her writing. Sadly I didn't enjoy the first installment. At all. <br/><br/>I found the Duke of Avon to be a rather fashionable reptile with a fan (yes, you read th</span>
  <span id="freeText12618332039828728138" style="display:none">I'm a fan of romance novels, especially historical, so I tend to read quite a bit of them. I know that Georgette Heyer is sort of a legend in this subgenre, but I have never read any of her books before now. I chose to read <i>These Old Shades</i> because it's part of a trilogy. I thought, hey, I'll read the three books and then decide what I think of her writing. Sadly I didn't enjoy the first installment. At all. <br /><br />I found the Duke of Avon to be a rather fashionable reptile with a fan (yes, you read that right). Do not get me wrong, I enjoy these fashionable anti-heroes (see Eloisa James' the Duke of Villiers), but Heyer's Avon felt rather cardboard. There wasn't much to him really, apart his vapid need for revenge and calling Leonie "my infant", which made me very, very uncomfortable. <br /><br />Now, Leonie. Apparently she's nineteen. I disagree. I believe that the girl has the emotional and and intellectual maturity of a teenage girl. I'd give her fifteen at most. But that isn't the worst part. That was Leonie's obnoxiousness and tendency to call everyone stupid. She's just extremely annoying and silly. The moment she opened her mouth, I wanted her to shut up. I admit I wanted to strangle her upon occasion. I didn't really see anything deeper inside her personality as Avon did. Leonie's really just an infant. <br /><br />As to the romance between Avon and Leonie, all I can say is that, <i>boy, am I skeeved</i>. This pairing just did not work for me; there just wasn't any chemistry between the protagonists. Also, the age difference just made my skin crawl. And that, believe me, is quite an achievement, because age differences between couples have never fazed me before. I also don't give a damn if it's the man or the woman (if it's hetero romance) who's older. But this time it just felt so wrong. It's not that Avon is twenty-plus years older than Leonie (and a reptile), but rather that she has the maturity of a kid, despite her being nineteen. Honestly, it felt like Avon himself saw her as a child, calling her "my infant" all the time. Even after their unfortunate nuptials. Eww. <br /><br />Soooo... one down, two to go, and then I'll make my decision whether to read more of Heyer's work. But really, I'm hoping that this one was just an odd miss and I'll enjoy the other two in this trilogy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12618332039828728138" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3586591950" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3586591950" />
    <a title="Abigail Bok" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32345761-abigail-bok"><img alt="Abigail Bok" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442980475p2/32345761.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3586591950?book_show_action=true">Oct 11, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Abigail Bok" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Abigail Bok" href="/user/show/32345761-abigail-bok">Abigail Bok</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3586591950" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6981842598102066913"><i>These Old Shades</i> is in some ways a rewrite of Heyer’s first novel, <i>The Black Moth.</i> It shows both how far she came in her skills over a few short years, and how far she had yet to go. Like <i>The Black Moth,</i> its hero is a hardened, vicious older man with a reputation for uncanny perspicacity; but the heroine of <i>These Old Shades</i> is miles ahead of her predecessor in interest and originality. And Heyer’s focus, instead of being solely on the hero, goes back and forth a bit here between hero and heroine</span>
  <span id="freeText6981842598102066913" style="display:none"><i>These Old Shades</i> is in some ways a rewrite of Heyer’s first novel, <i>The Black Moth.</i> It shows both how far she came in her skills over a few short years, and how far she had yet to go. Like <i>The Black Moth,</i> its hero is a hardened, vicious older man with a reputation for uncanny perspicacity; but the heroine of <i>These Old Shades</i> is miles ahead of her predecessor in interest and originality. And Heyer’s focus, instead of being solely on the hero, goes back and forth a bit here between hero and heroine. In later books she largely avoided telling stories from the hero’s point of view—a sign that she was coming to understand her audience.<br /><br />The scene opens on the Duke of Avon strolling down a Paris street (the year is about 1760) late at night. Suddenly a slim youth rushes out of a dark alley and crashes into him. The child, however, is not bent on robbery; he is fleeing an abusive brother and sister-in-law. On what appears to be a whim (but isn’t because, you know, the whole uncanny perspicacity thing), the duke buys the youth from his brother. He takes the child to his Paris home and sets him up as a page.<br /><br />The young page, Léon, proves to be a spunky kid who idolizes his rescuer but also challenges him impertinently at every turn. He is convincingly a child of the streets, manipulative, bloodthirsty, and a bit amoral. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[What he is <i>not</i> convincingly is a boy—it soon becomes apparent that Léon is really Léonie. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> And she bears a striking resemblance to the duke’s worst enemy.<br /><br />Léonie leaps off every page with energy; she rarely fails to surprise, and she lifts the story out of the mire of costume melodrama. Her relationship with the duke is wildly unconventional but works for them, and she forces us to see her stock antihero with new eyes.<br /><br />Heyer’s youth as a writer can be seen in the breathlessness of the plot, the obsession with matters of honor and revenge, and the ease with which many of the sophisticated aristocrats of the story follow the duke’s lead. But her growing skills are apparent in the secondary characters, who provide leaven to the drama and make the story more human and relatable. The duke’s brother Rupert is especially a standout. I wish Heyer had not felt the need to give so many characters names beginning with <i>M,</i> which forced me to stop and reflect periodically on who was who. But the tale is lively enough that I gave up questioning plausibility and just went with the fantasy, with very satisfying results. And this book has the added benefit of being the prequel to one of my all-time favorite Heyers, <i>Devil’s Cub.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="6981842598102066913" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2839472922" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2839472922" />
    <a title="Julie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11728765-julie"><img alt="Julie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1558426644p2/11728765.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2839472922?book_show_action=true">May 29, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie" href="/user/show/11728765-julie">Julie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11728765-julie?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2839472922" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12972553001640128256">This book captured me from the start, barreling into the story just as Leon barrells into the Duke. The Duke’s machinations form the basis of the plot, but it’s the characters and their relationships which give the story it’s considerable charm. <br/><br/>I found Leonie adorable. I loved her language (I had to smile every time she called someone a “pig-person”), her bloodthirsty streak, and her utter devotion to the Duke. Although occasionally this made her seem a bit like an over-enthusiastic puppy, I th</span>
  <span id="freeText12972553001640128256" style="display:none">This book captured me from the start, barreling into the story just as Leon barrells into the Duke. The Duke’s machinations form the basis of the plot, but it’s the characters and their relationships which give the story it’s considerable charm. <br /><br />I found Leonie adorable. I loved her language (I had to smile every time she called someone a “pig-person”), her bloodthirsty streak, and her utter devotion to the Duke. Although occasionally this made her seem a bit like an over-enthusiastic puppy, I thought she was delightful, enlivening the pages and the Duke’s life with her irrepressible ways. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[As for the age gap between these two, yes, twenty years is significant. But it’s nowhere near as repugnant as the custom of earlier times, of marrying women off whilst scarcely more than children. Despite her childlike behaviour in many cases, Leonie is nineteen, and has lived far from a sheltered life.<br /><br />I think Heyer sometime asks of us that we suspend judgement as well as disbelief. Has she achieved it here? The answer, of course, will vary for each reader.<br /><br />I have to admit that the continued use of “infant” as an endearment, and the guardian/ward relationship gave me some qualms about them ending up as a couple. I like that Heyer didn’t shy away from the question, either; she shows Avon as reluctant to put their relationship on a another footing because of it. But Fanny didn’t see it as any impediment. And really, could we imagine Leonie ending up with anyone other than her Monseigneur? Why, she can scarcely let the man out of her sight. So, to the age gap, as Leonie would say: “Ah, bah.” For these two particular characters, given their background and experiences, and the way each touched a chord in the other that no one else could, I was prepared to suspend judgement and even practicalities - we see, for example, in Devil’s Cub, that the Duke is an old man while Leonie is still in her prime - and allow that yes, perhaps they do belong together. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />And as the story progresses, Avon proves himself unable to resist Leonie’s relentless adoration. And who could blame him? But there’s more it than that, and his time with her changes him. Not the cold, calculating facade he turns towards everyone else; with Leonie he is different. His attempts to chastise and control her worst outbursts are priceless, becoming as they do ever more indulgent and affectionate. And I like how we see, over time, that his motive for seeking to bring down Saint-Vire is no longer for personal wrongs, but for the injustices which his enemy has done to Leonie, and for the type of life to which he has wilfully subjected her. <br /><br />Then the interactions between Rupert and Leonie were humorous, and added another dimension to the story. And I liked how the Duke’s other relationships were shown too during the course of the book, both with his siblings, and with his friend Hugh.<br /><br />So overall this was a book whose characters had real appeal, and in my opinion it deserves each of its five stars. I’m sure it’s one that I’ll read again one day, and that I’ll enjoy it equally as much.<br /><br />October 2020<br />Re-read with the Heyer group. The prediction proved true, keeps all its stars! </span>
  <a data-text-id="12972553001640128256" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1270422076" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1270422076" />
    <a title="Seema Khan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19611464-seema-khan"><img alt="Seema Khan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1493197946p2/19611464.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1270422076?book_show_action=true">Aug 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Seema Khan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Seema Khan" href="/user/show/19611464-seema-khan">Seema Khan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11539382-these-old-shades">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone looking for a touching and lasting tale of love!</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19611464-seema-khan?shelf=favourite">favourite</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19611464-seema-khan?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19611464-seema-khan?shelf=georgette-heyer">georgette-heyer</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19611464-seema-khan?shelf=romantic">romantic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19611464-seema-khan?shelf=there-ought-to-be-a-movie-on-this">there-ought-to-be-a-movie-on-this</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19611464-seema-khan?shelf=must-read">must-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19611464-seema-khan?shelf=unmatched-writing">unmatched-writing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19611464-seema-khan?shelf=awesome-characters">awesome-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19611464-seema-khan?shelf=my-fav-hero">my-fav-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19611464-seema-khan?shelf=my-fav-heroine">my-fav-heroine</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1270422076" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer999047728804602159">This review is just a picture of how personally I take my books and how involved I get! Great many spoilers and fan girl babbling ahead!<br/><br/><br/>Now I don’t know how this happened but it was just a coincidence that I read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/311322.The_Black_Moth' title='The Black Moth by Georgette Heyer' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Black Moth</a> before reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/311182.These_Old_Shades__Alastair___1_' title='These Old Shades (Alastair, #1) by Georgette Heyer' rel='nofollow noopener'>These Old Shades</a> and I hadn’t read any of the blurbs about these books before beginning them either. While I read it, there was some clicking going on in my mind that something is familiar, that I know some of these things. I also felt that Satanas was so s</span>
  <span id="freeText999047728804602159" style="display:none">This review is just a picture of how personally I take my books and how involved I get! Great many spoilers and fan girl babbling ahead!<br /><br /><br />Now I don’t know how this happened but it was just a coincidence that I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/311322.The_Black_Moth" title="The Black Moth by Georgette Heyer" rel="nofollow noopener">The Black Moth</a> before reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/311182.These_Old_Shades__Alastair___1_" title="These Old Shades (Alastair, #1) by Georgette Heyer" rel="nofollow noopener">These Old Shades</a> and I hadn’t read any of the blurbs about these books before beginning them either. While I read it, there was some clicking going on in my mind that something is familiar, that I know some of these things. I also felt that Satanas was so similar to The Duke of Andover, the Devil. Further Anthony Merivale is very much alike Sir Anthony Ferndale, in that he had some highwayman history to his name, and had rescued his wife Jennifer from Satanas while he was abducting her and also had had a terrific sword fight with him that was played with almost the same level of expertise, though Merivale had a slight edge over Avon (remember Jack taught fencing in France?) Now weren’t all these actions what had also ensued between Sir Anthony Ferndale and the Duke of Andover? Further the character of Hugh Devanant is again similar to Devil’s friend who unwaveringly is focused on reforming Devil and is seen prophesying that he will one day love someone more than himself. I felt curious and I then did some research. It turns out that Heyer had written These Old Shades using the same characters, retaining their character essence in their names and just made them more three dimensional. And it indeed is another side to the story of The Black Moth (set three years after the happenings of The Black moth) and it was said that she had named the book as she did in order to give it a continuation of sorts. <br /><br /><br />I did not like The Black Moth as much as I have liked other Heyer books; in fact I have listed it in my bottom 5 Heyers recently. But after having read TOS, I am fascinated! There can be no other book like These Old Shades! I love it to the last shred! And that is an understatement! I just cannot understand how this was penned. The detailing of emotions, actions, feelings and situations is just out of the world!<br /><br /><br />First, It is Monseigneur and Léon, the page!<br /><br />Oh such a cute mix of loyalty, devotion, love, servitude, fury in Léon and of an apparently detached interest, care, admonition and command in Satanas. This phase in their lives was so pure and unadulterated. I was touched at Léon’s selfless and zealous dedication to Avon and his fury in defense of his master. Léon’s rescue at the hands of Avon from the clutches of Jean and his horrid wife, have earned for the Duke a lifelong dedicated and devoted servant. Léon has placed his Monseigneur on a pinnacle of heroism.<br /> <br /><br />Here, It always goes like:<br /><br /><br />Avon: Do this! (With haughtiness)<br />Léon: Yes, Monseigneur!<br />Avon: We go to Vaussauds! <br />Léon: Yes, Monseigneur!<br />Avon: an impertinent page!<br />Léon: (engaging smile)<br />Avon: My Léon (Oh, how cute!)<br />Léon: I will be yours forever My Monseigneur! <br />Avon: My infant! (How endearing!)<br />Léon: You are the best Monseigneur!<br /><br /><br />Then the covers are lifted and truth revealed to Avon (though he’s known it forever!) Léon turns into Léonie and is taught to be a girl again and becomes Avon’s ward.<br /><br /><br />Then it is Monseigneur and Léonie, the ward!<br /><br /><br />Oh there’s growth in this phase. Growth in love, in devotion, in care and in affections and fondness of Léonie and Avon for each other. It’s not just Léonie who is fond of him; there is also growth in Avon’s attachment here. And there’s not just fondness, but a mutual respect evident. I had a lump in the throat and almost cried at a couple of places. Some of the best scenes I have ever read are in this book, especially the one where Avon leaves Léonie in Lady Fanny’s care. That’s my favourite scene. Then, the travel to and from Versailles. Also, Léonie and Avon’s reunion in Bassincourt. <br /><br />What we come across in this phase is:<br /><br />Léonie: Monseigneur do this! (With an engaging smile)<br />Avon: Yes infant!<br />Léonie: Monseigneur not our library! (a captivating dimple here)<br />Avon: Yes, ma fille!<br />Léonie: Monseigneur not that! (an ensnaring peep from beneath the lashes)<br />Avon: yes my child!<br /><br /><br />So basically, she has Avon around her little finger! Satanas, whom no one could prevail upon finally comes to love someone more than himself! <br /><br /><br />I never thought I’d say this, but: “I love Satanas!” I mean who could not?? For all his satanical actions, I still find His Grace of Avon, Justin Alastair one of the most charming and endearing heroes ever! He is enthralling and fascinating. The sarcasm and the sharp straight-faced one-liners are just too good! Under the façade of his satanical acts, there is a human aspect to Justin which only Leonie succeeds in nudging out. His kindness, empathy and care for Leonie are remarkably beautiful. He is aware of his own unworthiness and is trying his best to save Léonie from himself. His anguish and accumulating vengeance for what Léonie has had to suffer for her father’s vile actions is captivating to read. To revenge Léonie’s sufferings he, at one point forgets that he himself had a score to settle with Saint Vire so taken is he by her and so selfless is his love.<br /><br /><br />Léonie or Léon! She is my most beloved of Heyer heroines, even more than Frederica and Venetia whom I had found the most likable up till now. Reading TOS has really changed the sequence of my favourites. She is just so selfless in her love for Justin and so devoted to him. There’s nothing she won’t do for him. The sweet mix of innocence, wisdom and cynicism and her defense of her master with all her life and heart are just so cute! “I am his dog” – who says this? I mean this is the height of innocent devotion! Her reminiscence of the small conversational details they have had, her fear of losing him, of being away from him and unhappiness at being parted from him when he’s on his travels, her whim of keeping the library out of reach of outsiders just because it is ‘their’ sitting place and where he had brought her for the first time are the things which really show how much he means to her and how much each moment they passed together is important to her. <br /><br /><br />Such intricate description of the small nothings which are valued as everything endears the book so much to the heart!<br /><br />I found their love for one another selfless and unadulterated. There is a sense of belonging between them right from their first meeting with each other and their bond just grows stronger each moment. And it was not just Justin and Léonie, but Monseigneur and Léon were equally beautiful. “My Leon” and “Monseigneur” are just simple endearments denoting such deep fondness, pride and affection. They are just made for each other!<br /><br /><br />Hugh Devanant, Lord Rupert Alastair, Lady Fanny Marling who have substantial roles to play in the story are all so very likable. Rupert’s outspoken jests are hilarious! Lady Fanny is a sweet heart and Hugh Devanant such a level headed and caring friend. Merivale is interesting and I felt like killing Saint Vire myself! (Told you I get too involved!)<br /><br /><br />The story is compelling. The way it is wrought is remarkable. Splendid, in fact! No doubt, it is so loved and appreciated around the globe.<br /><br /><br />I could go on and on and on about it and still not be satisfied with what I’ve written because this is not even a tenth of what I feel! I’ve come to love and appreciate Georgette Heyer even more after this and am royally spoilt for other books!<br /><br /><br />I would just say: IF YOU HAVEN’T READ THIS BOOK, YOU’VE LEFT A BEAUTIFUL TREASURE UNOPENED. A MUST READ IN THIS LIFETIME!<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="999047728804602159" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Amy S" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1010492-amy-s"><img alt="Amy S" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1502458434p2/1010492.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/852183714?book_show_action=true">Feb 11, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy S" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy S" href="/user/show/1010492-amy-s">Amy S</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781402219474" href="/book/show/6807878-these-old-shades">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer852183714" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7619608039150108044">While I am not a tremendous Heyer fan, I do enjoy knocking them back like m&ms. That probably doesn't make sense to anyone but me. So by that I mean, like m&ms they don't have a lot of substance or weight, and it really annoys me that I keep eating them, and yet I can't seem to stop.<br/><br/>My understanding is that this is one of her first novels. It concerns Justin, the Duke of Avon, and Leone who -- whoopsie -- turns out to be Leonie. The Duke of Avon is supposed to be a first class rake of low reputa</span>
  <span id="freeText7619608039150108044" style="display:none">While I am not a tremendous Heyer fan, I do enjoy knocking them back like m&amp;ms. That probably doesn't make sense to anyone but me. So by that I mean, like m&amp;ms they don't have a lot of substance or weight, and it really annoys me that I keep eating them, and yet I can't seem to stop.<br /><br />My understanding is that this is one of her first novels. It concerns Justin, the Duke of Avon, and Leone who -- whoopsie -- turns out to be Leonie. The Duke of Avon is supposed to be a first class rake of low reputation, nicknamed "Satanas." However, we never quite learn what he has done to deserve this nickname, and because of that it was hard for me to believe he was really that bad. He is always impeccably dressed and mannered, and I cannot tell you how much I enjoyed his razor-sharp wit. No one can so elegantly put someone in their place like the Duke. <br /><br />Leonie is young, young, young, rough around the edges as she's been raised a boy, and quite the ingenue, which was annoying at times, but her sincerity and earnestness saved the day. <br /><br />The other characters in the book were quite a bit of fun as well: Justin's sister Fanny was a riot, and Rupert his brother the comic relief. Although with that it bugged me a bit as I am no fan of Heyer's slang. <br /><br />Speaking of slang, the best thing about this book is that the word "odious" did not appear once.<br /><br />This is a book where I truly was unsure of how it would end. I was not sure the hero/heroine would be together or if they should be. I enjoyed all the twists and turns, even though a bit of the book dragged for me somewhere in the middle. But as I have no problem skipping through sections of a book, it didn't hamper me too much. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7619608039150108044" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_159657805" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/159657805" />
    <a title="Amy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2329228-amy"><img alt="Amy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1433629372p2/2329228.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/159657805?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy" href="/user/show/2329228-amy">Amy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780373773404" href="/book/show/3405157-these-old-shades">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2329228-amy?shelf=georgette-heyer">georgette-heyer</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2329228-amy?shelf=re-read-in-2017">re-read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2329228-amy?shelf=favorite-characters">favorite-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2329228-amy?shelf=re-read-in-2019">re-read-in-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2329228-amy?shelf=re-read-in-2020">re-read-in-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2329228-amy?shelf=books-i-have-re-read-time-and-time">books-i-have-re-read-time-and-time</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer159657805" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16184117911915189823"><b>2020 Review </b><br/>I just...I <i>laugh out loud.</i> Even knowing the lines are coming. Even already having read them 4 times. I can't help myself. I giggle helplessly every time I hit the scene with the guy with the stolen horse. <br/><br/><b>2019 Review </b><br/>Squeeeeaaaaaalllllll. <br/>Major fangirling. Lovely re-read. Happy Amy.<br/><br/><b>March 29, 2017 Review </b> 5 stars<br/>It causes me almost physical pain re-reading my review from 2011...I must apologize. I was so young. However, on principle, I don't change reviews, only add to them. So here i</span>
  <span id="freeText16184117911915189823" style="display:none"><b>2020 Review </b><br />I just...I <i>laugh out loud.</i> Even knowing the lines are coming. Even already having read them 4 times. I can't help myself. I giggle helplessly every time I hit the scene with the guy with the stolen horse. <br /><br /><b>2019 Review </b><br />Squeeeeaaaaaalllllll. <br />Major fangirling. Lovely re-read. Happy Amy.<br /><br /><b>March 29, 2017 Review </b> 5 stars<br />It causes me almost physical pain re-reading my review from 2011...I must apologize. I was so young. However, on principle, I don't change reviews, only add to them. So here is my addition: <br />For many years, I have viewed <i>These Old Shades</i> as my least favorite of my favorite Heyer novels. While I have read and re-read her other works, I've generally avoided this one. <br />Which probably was a good thing for me.<br />Now that I'm older, I view this book in a totally different light. It is utterly charming. Justin Alastair is swoon worthy and Leonie is memorable and fantastic. Their romance is sweet and lovely. There are so many memorable, fun characters. <br />*content sigh* <br />Really, this book was remarkably good. I need to buy it. Like, now. <br /><br />..........................................................................<br /><br /><b>April 7th, 2011 Review</b> 3 stars<br /><br />Have you read <i> These Old Shades </i> by Georgette Heyer? <br />My, how droll of you, but you verily must. I tell you, you haven’t read <i> Heyer </i> until you’ve read this one. It has got a bit of everything and is a very sweet romance at that! <br /><br />Justin Alastiar, Duke of Avalon, takes pride in his nickname, Satanas. He is a coldhearted man, known for scandal and vice, disliked by just about everyone. When he buys (“body and soul”) a red-headed youth from the streets to serve as his page, everyone presumes it is just another of his mad whims. Who brings a page everywhere, anyway? But Avalon has suspected what only a very few know, and that is this supposed farm urchin “Leon” is really “Leonie”, the legitimate and wronged daughter of his hated enemy, the Comte de Saint Vire, whose mad desire for a son led him to disown his very child. Determined to get his revenge on Saint Vire by bringing abject humiliation, Avalon adopts the child (now properly made Leonie) and sets her up to destroy her own Father. What he did not expect was the beautiful transformation of the young girl, whose heart of gold may be just the thing to melt Satanas’s heart of stone…<br />I began this book…warily. While Heyer apparently has no problem setting up heroes with a past (look at <i> Frederica </i> or <i> Arabella </i>) never has is it quite as obviously flaunted. Of course, you need to in this case. The Duke of Avalon rather deserves his nick-name. But still…I was wary.<br />And I’d recommend reading the book like that, with half an eye out. I was less distracted by his vices because I was <i> expecting </i> them. And it really isn’t too bad. Just a note if warning there, then. <br />Actually, I quite deplored the two main characters, Avalon and Leonie. Deplored I say! xD (deplored is such a fun word) They were delightfully well done and yet I dislike both of them excessively! While I wanted them to get together, I didn’t like them <i> personally </i>. Which is probably what makes Heyer’s writing so remarkable, you can dislike a character and still root for them. Avalon was a licentious profligate (more fun words) whose main interests seem to be in revenge, his various mistresses, and his clothing. <br />Leonie is more difficult to pin down, because she hides behind a mask. Avalon is the only one who recognizes that under heir air of innocence and impishness is a hurt, unloved young woman. That is part of what makes their romance so sweet. Everyone sees her bouncy exterior, but he recognizes her for who she really is and, as his character changes, begins to love her for it. I got tired with her duped innocence, though. I don’t think it was “faked”, but it got irritating after a while. The story hints that she gained a bit of the Duke’s haughtiness, but she doesn’t seem to have gotten much brighter.<br />Here is a bit of an example of what her character is like: <br />On the night of all ball hosted in her honor with all of fashionable Paris turning out, she is dressed to the nines and glamorously makes her entrance into their immediate circle of friends…when they don’t immediately behold her, she pauses on the stairs, unfurls her fan, and says reprovingly,<br /><i> “But look at me!” </i><br />Which is followed by her skipping (or perhaps it is dancing, she seems to “dance about the room” a great deal) down the remaining stairs and onto her guardian’s arm. Quaint comments like “but look at me!” seem to <i>stress</i> what a dear, quaint, innocent creature she is….even as you learn what she has been to and how very “un-innocent” she is. <br />And so you see the double mask painted with her, hiding behind being a “quaint darling” and the “latest goddess of Paris”, while secretly struggling with pain and fear and longing. <br />So while her “innocence” got on my nerves and while Avon’s past was really a bit of a turn-off, by the end of the book they have gone through quite a bit of character change, greatly for the better. (I still didn’t <i> like </i> them but they were much better xD) <br />The secondary characters in this book, though, were excellent! Very memorable, from Avon’s sister Fanny and younger brother Rupert, to his dear friend Hugh, to Fanny’s husband, to his English neighbors who dislike him personally but are quite fond of Leonie…even to Leonie’s biological uncle or Conde, the Prince who finds her charming, it is such a mixed bunch of good characters! You can’t <i> help </i> but like ‘em! <br />This book has a bit of everything. Kidnapping, chase, betrayal, a landowner’s best beaver cap! It is a beautifully created world of royal France and polite England, of counts and dukes and duels! Oh it is lovely. <br />The story itself is almost a fairytale; the young, wrongly-abused girl plucked from the streets and made a princess. The romance was adorable and, I think, believable. If you are rather distraught t the idea of a 40-year-old man with a history marrying a 20-year-old (as I certainly was!), it is handled well. <br />I would like to make one last comment…I am rather flabbergasted how many reviewers consider Avalon the best Heyer hero. Sure, he has many elements of sweetness and awareness (“I know women”, he frequently states) but <i> the best </i>??? Ah well, to each his own. <br />Would I recommend this book? Yes. I would. To an older audience, mind you, and I probably wouldn’t go out of my way to recommend it, but you really haven’t read Heyer until you’ve read this one. It isn’t my favorite (I still prefer <i>The Grand Sophy</i> and <i> Frederica </i> and maybe even <i> Cotillion </i>) but it is excellent it its own way. <br /><br />So read warily, it is comic and romantic, but...older. At least that is what this teenager says. Very much a romance novel (with action thrown in)<br /><br /><br />(EDIT: oh, and why does the book have the same cover as "The Grand Sophy"? Most peculiar.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="16184117911915189823" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/676443" />
    <a title="Res" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56479-res"><img alt="Res" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/676443?book_show_action=true">Apr 11, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Res" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Res" href="/user/show/56479-res">Res</a>
      </span>

        rated it

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56479-res?shelf=romance">romance</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer676443" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5802321014280497514">The character of Leonie is immensely likeable (though, like Amanda in Sprig Muslin, she'd make more sense as a 15-year-old than at her stated age, which is 19). I don't quite see in her what Avon says he sees, the results of a life of terrible, constant loneliness.<br/><br/>Avon is more problematic. Partly it's a Georgian-culture problem -- it's hard for me to distinguish between an ordinary, irresponsible nobleman of fashion and an actual rake in the old, non-playful sense of the word. We know he kidnapp</span>
  <span id="freeText5802321014280497514" style="display:none">The character of Leonie is immensely likeable (though, like Amanda in Sprig Muslin, she'd make more sense as a 15-year-old than at her stated age, which is 19). I don't quite see in her what Avon says he sees, the results of a life of terrible, constant loneliness.<br /><br />Avon is more problematic. Partly it's a Georgian-culture problem -- it's hard for me to distinguish between an ordinary, irresponsible nobleman of fashion and an actual rake in the old, non-playful sense of the word. We know he kidnapped Jenny Merivale as a youth, though evidently he left her marriageable; we know Jenny and her husband won't associate with him, and neither will his sister Fanny's husband, or, we take it, most people of morals, except, for some reason, Hugh Davenant. We know he's nicknamed Satanas; when he declares his love for Leonie, he makes a touching confession of having an unclean heart ... but we never really see or hear reports of specific behaviours that so much set him apart from other men of his set. (Except, I suppose, intentionally provoking a rival to suicide, but this is set up in such a way that you cheer it.)<br /><br />Gender assumptions (Leonie is universally admired for the frankness that comes of having been raised as a boy) and class ones (she's still recognizably a Lady, and the switched baby a peasant, despite their upbringings) are hard to ignore, and as always with gender-switch stories, I feel like the homoeroticism is raised and then hastily shoved offstage again.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5802321014280497514" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15567333637207025543">I enjoyed this Heyer novel, but not as much as I was expecting to. <br/><br/>First of all, I'm a Regency girl.   <span id="freeText15567333637207025543" style="display:none">I enjoyed this Heyer novel, but not as much as I was expecting to. <br /><br />First of all, I'm a Regency girl. Georgian era powdered wigs and high-heeled frou-frou men are just not my cuppa tea. The Duke, Justin, is nicknamed Satan. He's a rake. I always love villains, right? Well, Monsigneur is a POSEUR VILLAIN who wears Nancy pants! <br /><br />I did love Leonie. She had enough spark and mischief in her to keep her from being a Mary Sue. Supporting cast was magnifique! <br /><br />I was surprised to discover that I understood all the French dialogue. I took four years of Français a million years ago in middle school and had a French pen-pal. I thought I was so fluent! In fourth year, Madam Fitz had us watch Gigi and French commercials. What are these people saying??? Quite a blow to my ego. I promptly changed my flag from Francophile to Anglophile upon discovering Jane Austen a few years later and still want to be a Brit. True story mon amies...er..mates.<br /><br />A solid 3 star read. I guess I need to love the hero in order to give all the stars.</span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3684666458247150732">I'm finding the protagonists quite distasteful -- actually morally reprehensible, rather than merely "not to my taste" -- and their relationship creepy and unhealthy. From what I gather from other people who've read this, they don't have some catharsis or rupturing and become better people. And it isn't even witty in the usual Heyer manner. I'm dropping this one, at least until I am all out of other Heyer novels.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3015503-maria-grazia?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer191394789" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13611179888884100744"><i>“Set in the Georgian period, about 20 years before the Regency, These Old Shades is considered to be the book that launched Heyer’s career. It features two of Heyer’s most memorable characters: Justin Alastair, the Duke of Avon, and Leonie, whom he rescues from a life of ignomy and comes to love and marry”</i>.<br/><b>My review </b><br/>If you meet Satanas in a dark alley in the middle of the night and you are desperately seeking escape from a wretched life of violence and harassment, maybe you’d be as happy as youn</span>
  <span id="freeText13611179888884100744" style="display:none"><i>“Set in the Georgian period, about 20 years before the Regency, These Old Shades is considered to be the book that launched Heyer’s career. It features two of Heyer’s most memorable characters: Justin Alastair, the Duke of Avon, and Leonie, whom he rescues from a life of ignomy and comes to love and marry”</i>.<br /><b>My review </b><br />If you meet Satanas in a dark alley in the middle of the night and you are desperately seeking escape from a wretched life of violence and harassment, maybe you’d be as happy as young Leòn at becoming his, body and soul, bought for a diamond pin. Very happy to become his page and wear good clothes, to follow him wherever his libertine life led him without complaining, without questioning. <br />Especially if Satanas is just a nickname for a rich, elegant, fascinating nobleman: Justin Alastair, the Duke of Avon. And mainly if he appears to you like this:<br /><i>“ He walked mincingly, for the red heels of his shoes were very high. A long purple cloak, rose-lined, hung from his shoulders and was allowed to fall carelessly back from his dress, revealing a full-skirted coat of purple satin, heavily laced with gold; a waistcoat of flowered silk; faultless small clothes; and a lavish sprinkling of jewels on his cravat and breast”</i>.<br />Leòn’s new life as Avon’s page will lead the youth from a murky Parisian backstreet to the corrupt splendours of 18th century Versailles and the dignified mansions of England. If you were the young boy saved by the illustrious man from a horrible life of ill-treatmments, wouldn’t you admire him immensely, though everybody else considers him selfish, arrogant and even cruel? <br />This is precisely what Leòn starts doing. The child’s worshipping admiration for the Duke - Monseigneur, as he calls him – becomes amusement to the libertine’s old friends and, strangely enough, a menace to his old enemy, the Comte de Saint-Vire. In fact, the reason why the Duke bought Leòn was that he was struck by the boy's unusual colouring, which reminds him of his enemy's red hair and dark brows. <br />When Leòn is revealed to be Leonie , the story gets even more intriguing with the Duke making her his ward to be introduced at Versailles … (read this brilliant page online)<br />This is the beginning of an incredible series of enticing fast-paced adventures mingling intrigue, romance and the unmistakable Heyer mark, her incredible wit. A real romp to read all in one go to the very end.<br />What is incredible is that we have these incredible gripping characters taking shape under our eyes through their delightful dialogue exchanges and the incredible pressing flow of actions; all of them, even the secondary ones (i.e. Mr. Manvers, the Curé or Madame de Saint-Vire) are very neatly connoted , though only with a few thorough brushstrokes.<br />The two protagonists are outstanding and peculiar, though they have the trademark Heyer clearly printed on themselves. Justin Alastair is …<i>” known by the soubriquet Satanas, for his cold exactitude and prescient understanding of what his opponent will do next, as well as a certain elasticity in his moral fiber. The Duke has restored his family’s fortune through gambling; he is, as one would expect of one of the first peers of the realm, an arrant snob, careful, although certainly flamboyant, in his dress, and punctilious in manner” </i>(from Vic Sanborn’s review at Jane Austen’s World). <br />Someone told me Leonie is possibly Heyer’s least admired heroine. This sounds so impossible to me! However , I read that she is one of the characters Heyers herself loved most and I myself loved her immensely. Leonie is as loveable as flawed, a whirling personality, an oddly naïve female rogue, an irresistibly charming - though very little accomplished - young lady, ravishing beautiful and disarmingly stubborn, brave and fragile at the same time. If she can wrap the formidable Duke of Avon around her little finger with a smile and a gaze full of admiration under her lashes, how can we resist her ?<br />The plot is very well designed but readers need a great fix of … suspension of disbelief, of course. As for me, I’ve gone through the story with a constant smile on my face and making a great effort to put it down from time to time.<br /><b>These Old Shades</b> is the first book in the Alastairs Trilogy and I’m glad about it . This means there is more delight expecting me and many other willing readers out there, in <b>Devil’s Cub</b> and in <b>An Infamous Army</b>.<br />My review is on my blog too, FLY HIGH, at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://bit.ly/oDl2vT">http://bit.ly/oDl2vT</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13611179888884100744" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Jan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57282794-jan"><img alt="Jan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1505016022p2/57282794.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1684562307?book_show_action=true">Jun 30, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jan" href="/user/show/57282794-jan">Jan</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57282794-jan?shelf=british">british</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57282794-jan?shelf=georgian-era">georgian-era</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57282794-jan?shelf=france">france</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57282794-jan?shelf=clean">clean</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57282794-jan?shelf=age-gap">age-gap</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57282794-jan?shelf=omyw">omyw</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57282794-jan?shelf=cross-dressing">cross-dressing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57282794-jan?shelf=historical">historical</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1684562307" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3071337005132567198">It's hard to believe this book was first published in 1926. Almost 100 years ago. Wow. And it's hardly dated, although some of the dialogue does feel a little stilted or old-fashioned compared with 'modern' historical romances.<br/><br/>This book has to be one of the original cynical-rake-falls-for-good-woman-and-reforms-for-life tales, a much beloved HR trope still in 2020. It is is beautifully done, with Heyer's typical light touch. Leonie is such a charming, delightful character, and the mature Justin </span>
  <span id="freeText3071337005132567198" style="display:none">It's hard to believe this book was first published in 1926. Almost 100 years ago. Wow. And it's hardly dated, although some of the dialogue does feel a little stilted or old-fashioned compared with 'modern' historical romances.<br /><br />This book has to be one of the original cynical-rake-falls-for-good-woman-and-reforms-for-life tales, a much beloved HR trope still in 2020. It is is beautifully done, with Heyer's typical light touch. Leonie is such a charming, delightful character, and the mature Justin is perfect for her. The age gap between them is not a problem for me. Yes Leonie is young, but she has had some harsh experiences in her life that make her far from naive. And for her, Justin is able to grow and change his rakish ways. <br /><br />This story has it all. There is a deep and beautiful romance at its centre, but there is adventure, drama, humour, madcap journeys, gorgeous Georgian fashions, settings ranging from an English country house to the court of Versailles, and a great cast of secondary characters who you almost wish had their own books (Hugh Davenant for example).<br /><br />As with all Heyers, it's a clean read, but the romance is still wonderful. Just a look between the characters is enough to convey a world of feeling. The understatement leaves much to the reader's imagination, and it's a world away from the crudity of some of the more explicit HRs out there. This one is a charming, elegant, fast-moving, and still a very satisfying read after all these years.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3071337005132567198" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('A1fRWY2uQiB7j7sT159TFGto6OfQK06cAzkL5mpoiGvgZ63OZI+9b8qP6jRAYtnaiu1vAQp4m18QG//cybi8hA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Pn7RDEg1rcdY0ohRBphPWz7YSX3B3M8cH8oFI5DCyYjdTq2boRRSiOnS2XaRZcWV313OmxuPGt8M6PEZMxL9Zw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer3810898926989795794">Georgette Heyer was a prolific historical romance and detective fiction novelist. Her writing career began in 1921, when she turned a story for her younger brother into the novel <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/311322._The_Black_Moth' title=' The Black Moth' rel='nofollow noopener'> The Black Moth</a>.<br/><br/>In 1925 she married George Ronald Rougier, a mining engineer. Rougier later became a barrister and he often provided basic plot outlines for her thrillers. Beginning in 1932, Heyer released one romance nov</span>
  <span id="freeText3810898926989795794" style="display:none">Georgette Heyer was a prolific historical romance and detective fiction novelist. Her writing career began in 1921, when she turned a story for her younger brother into the novel <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/311322._The_Black_Moth" title=" The Black Moth" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Black Moth</a>.<br /><br />In 1925 she married George Ronald Rougier, a mining engineer. Rougier later became a barrister and he often provided basic plot outlines for her thrillers. Beginning in 1932, Heyer released one romance novel and one thriller each year.<br /><br />Heyer was an intensely private person who remained a best selling author all her life without the aid of publicity. She made no appearances, never gave an interview and only answered fan letters herself if they made an interesting historical point. She wrote one novel using the pseudonym Stella Martin.<br /><br />Her Georgian and Regencies romances were inspired by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1265._Jane_Austen" title=" Jane Austen" rel="nofollow noopener"> Jane Austen</a>. While some critics thought her novels were too detailed, others considered the level of detail to be Heyer's greatest asset.<br /><br />Heyer remains a popular and much-loved author, known for essentially establishing the historical romance genre and its subgenre Regency romance.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3810898926989795794" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
